- 32 -
5.02   Analysis of NWCPC's FY89/90 and FY90/91 financial statements also reveals that
revenues from operations have been far too low to permit the Corporation to adequately operate
and maintain its water schemes. It is only because depreciation was not as yet being charged on
its water scheme assets, as these assets have not been valued, and because NWCPC was not
paying any interest charges on loans which were incurred by MWD, that NWCPC generates a
positive net income. NWCPC's cash position is even tighter than the income statements suggest,
since water revenues collected In Mombasa and the Coastal Region, NWCPC's largest cost center
(accounting for about 90 percent of revenues), were only about 65 percent of billings during
FY89/90, due to the continuing billing of a large number of closed consumer accounts (para
4.19). This situation of inadequate revenues must be viewed in light of the fact that water tariffs
had not been increased since 1978 until the recent tariff revision which became effective on
October 1, 1991 (para 5.04). Although the average rate of increase is estimated to be about 50%,
further adjustments will be required to allow NWCPC to properly operate and maintain its water
schemes and service the debt associated with the proposed project.
5.03   NWCPC's assets and capital structure has not been fully established. Although a letter
from the Office of the Vice President and Ministry of Finance confirmed that the water scheme
assets would be transferred as an equity contribution and free of any encumbrances from MWD to
NWCPC (Ref. No: CONF, 3/08 (34) dated October 18, 1991), the values of the assets
transferred still need to be evaluated. NWCPC has also accorded high priority to resolving this
uncertainty concerning its capital structure and possible financial obligations and has prepared
terms of reference for a consultancy which will be supported under the Project to value the assets
and liabilities. These TORs were reviewed and agreed on by the Bank during preappraisal and are
included in Annex 9. NWCPC expects to retain a panel of three joint lead consultants, including
a civil engineer, a valuer and an accountant, to steer the valuation process, and their TORs were
reviewed by the Bank during preappraisal/appraisal and found acceptable. These TORs are also
included in Annex 9. The consultancy to value the assets and liabilities is scheduled to be
completed by end-FY92/93, at which time the valuations would be included in NWCPC's
financial statements. During negotiations agreement was reached that NWCPC would ensure that
the consultancy to value the assets and liabilities would be completed by no later than end-June,
1993.
W>ter Tariffs
5.04   As noted above, until recently water tariffs for MWD water schemes, including those
schemes transferred to NWCPC, had not been increased since 1978, despite continuing inflation
and inadequate revenues to support operating and maintenance costs. As a result, most water
schemes have been poorly maintained and many are in serious states of disrepair. Prior to the
negotiations the water tariffs for water schemes under the jurisdiction of both MWD and NWCPC
were increased by an estimated order of some 50% (versus a minimum 20% increase expected by
IDA) under The Water Act, Cap. 372, by legal notices Nos. 496, 497, 498, 499, 500, and 501,
effective as of October 1, 1991, published in the Kenya Gazette Supplement No. 654 dated
October 14, 1991.
5.05   The water tariff rates prior to the recent tariff increase effective as of October 1, 1991,
are summarized below:



- 33 -
Water Consumption          Mombasa/Coasa           Other Urban       _ural
per month                                   (KSh/m3)--------  ----------------
0 - 9m3                        2.90                     2,00        1.67
9m3 - above                      5.75                    2.00         2.65
Where no meters have been installed, domestic customers were to pay a charge of KSh 48 per
month in the Mombasa and the Coastal Region, KSh 30 per month in other urban areas and KSh
15 per month in rural areas. The new tariff rates are summarized in Annex 16.
5.06          Mombasa is a major tourist center and the second largest city in Kenya, and the
Mombasa and Coastal Region is the most sophisticated water supply system in the country outside
of Nairobi. A substantial portion (about 50 percent) of water usage is consumed by industrial,
commercial and hotel enterprises, but NWCPC had a uniform water tariff for all categories of
customers within areas and differentiates the tariffs only by two consumption levels. The average
incomes of its residential customers are estimated to be about the same as Nairobi, yet its average
tariff for Mombasa (about KSh 5/m3) was only about 60 percent of the prevailing average tariff
in Nairobi (about KSh 8/m3).
5.07          NWCPC and Government are aware that further substantial water tariff increases
will still be required over the medium term to generate sufficient internal funds to cover operating
and maintenance costs, provide adequate debt service coverage for the proposed project and to put
NWCPC on a sound financial footing so that it will be in a position to borrow the large expected
loans for, and generate enough funds to contribute to the capital cost of, the follow-on main
investment project. During negotiations agreement was reached that Government would approve
and NWCPC would implement such tariff increases as necessary beginning in FY92/93 so that
total revenues from NWCPC's water supply services will be sufficient to meet all operations,
maintenance, and interest expenses in each fiscal year as well as 40 percent of depreciation in
FY92/93, 65 percent of depreciation in FY93/94 and 100 percent of depreciation in FY94/95 and
thereafter and provide a reasonable contribution (i.e. not less than 10 percent of the projected
annual cost of the acquisition of assets for expansion of NWCPC's operations) to reserves by
FY94/95 and each fiscal year thereafter. The impact of the tariff increases would be analyzed at
the end of March in each fiscal year to determine the rate of the next increase. It is expected that
large tariff increases (roughly of the order of magnitude of 35-50 percent per year in nominal
terms) will be required over the medium term to meet the financial objectives for NWCPC.
While the annual tariff increases may initially appear high, they are not considered unreasonable
when compared to inflation (as measured by the Nairobi CPI) which has exceeded 220 percent
over the past 13 years, during which time no tariff increases were implemented. With these
levels of tariff increases, water tariffs in Mombasa should approximate more closely those of
Nairobi by the time the follow-on main investment project is underway. Furthermore, after the
water tariff study (para 5.08) is completed, future water tariffs would be expected to be set in line
with economic considerations to better ensure the efficient allocation of resources in the sector.
5.08          Merely increasing the general level of tariffs will not address the issue of whether
the design of the tariff structure is the most economically efficient, whether it would maximize
revenue and whether it is consistent with other concerns - such as equity, administrative
convenience and cost of collection. Therefore, under the Project, consultants would be retained
to examine the tariff structure through a water tariff study. The study is expected to review the
appropriateness of uniform urban and uniform rural tariff structures versus regional and individual



- 34 -
water scheme tariff structures and the appropriateness of cross-subsidies through the tariff levels
and structures across and within regions. In addition, the ability to introduce greater
diff,rentiation of tariff structures would be examined, taking into consideration the mix of
government, hotel, industrial, commercial and domestic consumers within schemes and regions.
Lastly, the study would provide recommendations on the ways and means to protect the needs of
the lowest income groups through the tariff structure. The terms of reference (TORs) for the
water tariff study (included in the TORs for the Corporate Development Plan) were agreed with
NWCPC during appraisal and are shown in Annex 9. During negotiations agreement was reached
that the water tariff study, as part of the Corporate Development Plan (para 4.13), would be
completed by December 31, 1993.
Future Financial Performance
5.09         Projections of NWCPC's financial performance over the period FY91/92-
FY96/97, including income statements, sources and applications of funds statements and balance
sheets, are shown in Annex 12. The projections have been prepared assuming NWCPC would
introduce, beginning in FY92/93, further annual water tariff increases; the water scheme assets
would be transferred to NWCPC as an equity contribution; and the valuation of its water scheme
assets would be completeO by no later than end-June 1993 after which time depreciation will be
properly charged (see para 5.07). For the purpose of the analysis which was carried out jointly
with NWCPC, a notional value of the assets of KSh10.8 billion (US$400 million) was used.
Furthermore, water production in the Mombasa and Coastal Region is assumed to increase from
95,000 m3/day currently to 115,000 m3/day in FY91/92 when additional supply would become
available from a German-funded augmentation scheme and then to 155,000 m3/day mid-way
through FY93/94 when the proposed Project is expected to be essentially completed. Also, it has
been assumed that the terms of borrowed funds for the Project would carry an interest rate of
16.65 percent, with a maturity nf 20 years including a 5-year grace period.
5.10         With the introduction of agreed tariff increases (see para 5.07), the financial
projections indicate that NWCPC's financial position could gradually improve so that by the time
of the main investment project, NWCPC would be in a position to contribute at least 10 percent
of the capital cost of that project and service the large loans required as well as the loan for the
proposed Project. Interest coverage and the current ratio would be maintained well above
adequate levels of 1.5 and 2.0, respectively. Significant cash balances would accumulate during
the latter project years which would be required subsequently to supr!ort NWCPC's contribution
of at least 10 percent (roughly estimated at about US$20 million) of the .apital cost of the follow-
on main investment project as well as the costs of its other capital work-s. The operating ratio
(operating expenses/revenues) would decrease from about 68 percent pre;z-- ly to a more
acceptable level of about 27 percent by end-FY95/96. With replacement of faulty meters and
completion of the revenue collection improvement consultancy, overbilling of customers' accounts
would be expected to be eliminated. The water accounts in arrears would be expected to be
reduced from about 225 days presently to a more acceptable level of about 90 days by the end of
the project period. To properly monitor financial performance and to provide the basis for
determining water tariff increase requirements, agreement was reached during negotiations that,
on an annual basis beginning in FY91192, NWCPC would prepare a report, by no later than end-
March, containing six-year financial projections to be reviewed by the Association.

VI. PROJECT JUSTIFICATION
Projegt Benefits
6.01         The proposed Project would help the Govermnent and NWCPC in preparing a
Second Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Project to augment and secure the water supply
infrastructure in the region. The present water deficit of about 60 percent seriously affects not
only the population as a whole and the urban poor in particular, but also the economic
development and eatning capacity of the region, especially in the tourism industry, Kenya's
largest foreign exchange earner. The rehabilitation/augmentation of the existing water supply
facilities under this project are expected to reduce the water supply deficit to about 35 percent in
the short run and allow a more equitable distribution of the available water.
6.02         The Project would also provide support to NWCPC to ensure its institutional,
operational and financial viability for carrying out the proposed project in particular and for
fulfilling its broad mandate in the water supply sector in general.
6.03         In addition, the project would also ensure that adverse environmental impacts of
the follow-on project and of the rehabilitation/augmentation works under this Project would be
minimized, and the works would be carried out at minimum disturbance to the ecology.
Least Cost Solution
6.04         The preinvestment studies and engineering designs carried out under the proposed
Project would ensure that the least cost alternative would be selected for implementation under the
follow-on main investment project. The rehabilitation/augmentation work would significantly
improve the water supply situation in the region at minimal cost, and would improve the
operational reliability and efficiency of the system.
Economic Rate of Return
6.05         The estimated incremental project revenues 1/ were used as the measure of the
economic benefit of the Project. Incremental water revenues were valued at the proposed average
water tariffs calculated in real terms. Other benefits, including health benefits resulting from
improved water supply and benefits resulting from impact on urban development, tourism and
recreation were not quantifiable. All costs related to the augmentation/rehabilitation works (land,
civil works, equipment, engineering designs and construction supervision, physical contingencies
and recurrent costs were included in the analysis and adjusted to exclude taxes, interest charges
and inflation. Costs as well as benefits were considered over a 35 year period. On this basis, the
economic rate of return (ERR) was calculated at 23 percent. Shadow pricing the foreign
exchange and labor costs (using factors of 1.15 and 0.75 respectively) the Project yields an ERR
of 22 percent, the difference being less than the margin of error in the cost estimates. This, for
water supply projects unusually high ERR demonstrates the merits of the immediate improvement
measures included under the project.
1/ Generated by the sale of the additional water produced by the augmentation/rehabilItation
works.

PWoJect Risks
6.07         The introduction of an appropriate tariff policy which is expected to require
significant increases in current water tariffs could be difficult to achieve in view of political
constraints. To reduce this risk, the Project would provide for carrying out a tariff study and for
strengthening NWCPC's revenue collection and financial management systems. In addition, there
would be annual reviews in the Bank to agree on the following year's tariff requ,rements and
agreement was reached that the results of these analyses would be implemented and agreement
was reached that the results of the analysis of the annual tariff requirements would be
implemented. Government's firm commitment to the Project and to the objective of establishing
an independent, self-financing corporation was demonstrated by an initial tariff increase of about
50 percent, versus the minimum 20 percent required as a condition for negotiations. The
introduction of a differentiated, block tariff system lessened the impact of tariff increases on the
low income groups and would help to defuse the political/social issues of increasing the cost of
water for the consumers. Inadequate allocation in the Government's development budget for the
IDA Credit and counterpart funds due to financial and budgetary constraints would be another
risk. To reduce this risk a detailed schedule of the counterpart fund requirements had been
prepared jointly with NWCPC and Treasury, and agreement was reached that Government's
contribution would be deposited on the project account in a timely manner. The initial deposit
required for FY91192 was made a condition of Credit effectiveness. Some unforeseen difficulties
could arise from a relatively new institution in spite of its qualified staff, but these difficulties are
expected to be reduced through institutional support and the hiring of consultants to assist in
project preparation and implementation activities. Monitoring of NWCPC's performance in these
areas would be a fccus of IDA supervision.
Proiect Monitoring System
6.08      The key indicators to be monitored during implementation concern physical progress
of the project, operational performance of NWCPC, progress with actions on tariff and financial
performance of NWCPC. Suitable indicators for monitoring project implementation and for
measuritng performance are set out in Annex 15. After completion of the proposed Project,
NWCPC would prepare a 'Project Completion Report" on the basis of an outline to be agreed
with the Bank.

VII. AGREEMENTS R1EACHED AND RECOMMEN1DATION
Agreements Reachd During Negotiatiqns
7.01         During negotiations, the following agreements were reached:
(a)    Government would provide the counterpart contribution of 11 percent of
total project cost as an equity contribution to NWCPC (para 3.13);
(b)    Government would provide the portion of the IDA Credit utilized to
finance consultancy/advisory services under the institutional support
component, training, and preinvestment studies/engineering services for
the follow-on project ([JS$ 25.8 million equivalent) to NWCPC as an
equity contribution. The balance utilized to finance
rehabilitation/augmentation works (including associated engineering
services), vehicles and equipment (US$ 17.4 million equivalent) would be
on-lent to NWCPC as a loan at an interest rate of 16.65 percent per
annum. The loan to NWCPC would have a maturity of 20 years
including 5 years grace (para 3.14);
(c)   Government would provide in its annual development budget allocations
for the IDA Credit and counterpart funds for FY93 through FY96 in
accordance with an agreed schedule, and at the beginning of each quarter,
Government would deposit to the project account opened by NWCPC in a
commercial Bank the necessary amount to cover its contribution to the
local project expenditures during the quarter (para 3.15 (i) and (ii));
(d)    Government would establish and operate the Special Account for NWCPC
(para 3.24);
(e)   NWCPC would submit the Corporate Development Plan including the
tariff study for review and comment by the Association not later than
December 31, 1993 (paras. 4.13 and 5.08);
(f)    NWCPC would have its financial statements and its project account
audited by independent auditors acceptable to the Association and the audit
reports would be submitted to the Association within nine months of the
end of the fiscal year (para 4.16);
(g)    NWCPC would ensure that the consultancy to value the assets and
liabilities be completed by no later than end-June 1993 (para. 5.03);
(h)    Government would approve and NWCPC would take all necessary
measures including, without limitation, adjustment of the structure or level
of its tariffs, beginning in FY92/93 so that revenues from NWCPC's
water supply services will be sufficient to meet all operations,
maintenance, and interest expenses in each fiscal year as well as 40
percent of depreciation in FY92/93, 65 percent of depreciation in
FY93/94 and 100 percent of depreciation in FY94/95 and thereafter and



- 38 -
provide at least a 10% contribution to reserves by FY94/95 and each
fiscal year thereafter (para 5.07); and
(i)    NWCPC would, for the purpose of monitoring NWCPC's financial
performance and for determining water tariff increase requirements, on an
annual basis beginning in FY91/92, prepare a report by no later than end-
March containing six-year financial projections to be reviewed by the
Association (para 5.10).
Conditions of Credit Effectiveness
7.02         During negotiations agreements were obtained regarding the following conditions
of effectiveness:
(a)    execution of a Subsidiary Loan Agreement between Government and
NWCPC under terms and conditions acceptable to IDA (para 3.14);
(b)    counterpart contribution of US$820,000 equivalent in KSh for FY91/92
has been deposited by Government in an account opened by NWCPC in a
commercial bank (para 3.15, (ii)); and
(c)    establishing the Project Implementation Unit (PIU), which would be
headed by the Project Coordinator and would have four key staff, all with
terms of reference and'experience satisfactory to the Association (paras.
3.16 and 4.03).
Conditions for Disbursement
7.03         During negotiations, agreement was obtained regarding the following conditions
for disbursement:
(a)    NWCPC submitting a training program not later than March 31 of each
year, satisfactory to the Association, would be a condition for
disbursement for the training program in the following fiscal year (para
4.11); and
(b)    NWCPC submittin1, -a Environmental Action Plan, satisfactory to the
Association, for the I.v bilitation/augmentation works, would be a
condition for disbursement for the physical implementation of this
component (para. 3.25).
Rlecommndin
7.04         Subject to the above, the Proiect is suitable for an IDA Credit of US$43.2 million
equivalent at the standard IDA terms with a maturity of 40 years. The Borrower would be the
Government of Kenya.

A.
TERMS OF REFERENCE
FOR
VALUATION OF ASSETSILIABILITIES
INCLUDING CAPITAL STRUCTURE AND BALANCE SHEET
OBJECTIVES
The National Water and Conservation & Pipeline Corporation
wishes to carry out a comprehensive identification and
valuation of ali its assets and liabilities, to facilitate
the full and proper functioning of the corporation and with
particular reference to:
1.1.      Location,  identification    and  registration   of
assets.
1.2.      Maintenance, repair and replacement of assets.
1.3.      Assessment  and recording   of the  forms of  legal
title, together with any encumbrances thereto,
relating to assets.
1.4.      Insurance of assets against destruction or   damage
and insurance of the corporation against public
liability to third parties, arising from the
ownership, location end use of svch assets.
1.5.      Inspection  of certain   assets, particularly  dams
and similar structures, against potential safety
hazards.
1.6,      Assessment end  record of   physical and  financial
depreciation of assets, to facilitate planning for
replacement and the recording of depreciation in
accordance with standard accounting practices.
1.7.      Assessment  of  choices regarding   the  retention,
disposal,     replacement,      enhancement     and
rehabilitation of assets, based on appropriate
cost/benefit analysis.
1.8.     The  taking of  operational decisions   relating to
whiclh assets to operate at maximum capacity, as
contrasted with those to be held for standby or
reserve purposes.
1.9.      Assessment, for purposes   of financial performance
measurement, of the expected or actual financial
end economic returns from asset operation, for
comparison with the Corporation's cost of capital.
1.10.     Assessment of  the potential for the generation of
revenues from the operation, leasing or disposal
of assets.



-57-                         Annex 9
Page 2 of 32
.11.     Assessinent. of  all  l1:3bilities releting  to  the
assets, including:
1.9.1.    Lc.ny-term loans.
1.9.2.    Claims  by  cont.ract.ors,  donors,  self-help
organzations    arid  other    commlunities  or
indlviduals   claiming  not   to   have   been
adequately compensated   for t.he  provision or
financing of asset.s.
1.9.3.    Other cont-ingent liabilities.
1.10.    Assessment of financial and  other liabilities not.
directly related to the provision of assets,
including those to:
1.10.1.   Customers,  in respect  of consumer   deposits
and refunds due.
1.10.2.   Suppliers of goods and services.
1.10.3.   Banking and financing institutions.
1.10.4.   Central Government, other   public authorities
and ut.ilities.
1.1l.   As  a   consequence  of  the    identification  and
valuation of its assets and liabilities, the
Corporation wishes to prepare, for audit by its
stat.utory auditors, a  statement of affairs, drawn
up   in   accordance   with    generally   accepted
accounting principles and thereafter incorporated
into its books of account, so as to determine its
overall assets, liabilities and equity capital.
1.12.   In addition,  consistent   with its  position as  a
responsible public body, the CorForation wishes to
discharge its lawful obligations to its creditors.
It also wishes to hand over to their rightful
owners, or alternatively to compensate for, any
assets to which the Corporation has no legal
title.

2.   SPECIFICATION OF TASKS
2.1. Vluationof Assets
The assets of the Corporation consist, in the main, of
moveable  and    immoveable  installations,    pipelines,
plant, equipment,   stores, machinery,  dams, buildings,
vehicles, office furniture, etc. These are located at
the Corporation's water projects and    regional offices
and at its head offices in Nairobi. Comprehensive
valuation of these assets shell take into consideration
matters which, in the professional opinion of the
valuer, are relevant, with a view to advising the
Corporation on their current monetary value, in the
light of:
O    past working life and serviceability;
O    estimated remaining economic life; end,
O    changes   in  monetary  values  since   assets  were
purchased and/or put into service.
2.2.1.    Water Suplies._ ams and PL2elirs
Each of the operational water undertakings, dams
and   pipelines   shall   be  valued   t.aking  into
consideration the various components of the water
supply, such as, but not necessarily limited to:
O    intakes;
o    raw water mains;
O    treatment plants, where applicable;
O    pumping stations, where applicable;
O    power plants;
O    water     storage     facilities     (retaining
structures);
O    distribution   and  reticulation   systems  and
pipelines;
O    laboratory facilities, where applicable;
O    master consumer meters;
O    tools and equipment;
O    office buildings;
O    office furniture end equipment;
O    stores,   including  pipes,  fittings, meters,
parts etc;
O    workshops, where applicable;
O    yards end depots;
0    staff quarters; and,
O    transport facilities, where applicable.



Annex 9
_59_                             Page 4 of 32
While carrying out. the assessment, t.he Valuer must
teke  care to identify   and to differentiate those
installations which  have been  developed by   non-
MOWD agencies, such as self-help groups, NGOs, and
other institutions and   are now incorporated  into
the supply system.  A separate valuation   of these
assets is required.
For each of the above-named components, a thorough
and detailed assessment. of the value is required,
including a justification  and explanation of how
that value has been arrived at.
Whilst "as-built" dr-awings, hand-over reports,
contractors contract documents, etc. can provide
useful initial information for the valuer, the
Corporation will expect, as an integral part of
the valuation reports, updated maps showing routes
and location of principal installations. This will
require a significant amount of surveying, mapping
end drawing.
2.1.2.      ngQ   eational l4ndertakins
For undertakings currently under construction, the
valuers' assessment of the monetary value should
be guided by:
O    totel contract value for construction;
O    cost   of   pre-investment    and  feasibility
studies;
O    costs   of   design     and   supervision   of
constrvction;
O    administrative  end    legal  costs   properly
assessable against the fixed asset cost; and,
O    where  applicable,    for  long   construction
periods,   changes    in  money   values   and
financing costs during construction.
The Corporation operates the Dam Construction
Unit, together with its rigs and heavy machinery.
A full valuation of the Unit's machinery and rigs
shall be undertaken, with particular attention to:
O    depreciation;
O    current  state   and   serviceability  of the
machinery and equipment; and
O    current  disposal values   as used  equipment,
compared  with  current    market  values  for
replacement.

2.1.4.    Heedquarters and Regiona1 Offices
A full valuation of tthe moveable and immovable
asset.s held by the Corporation at its Headquarters
and at. its various Regional Offices shall be
carried out, including, but not. limited to:
0    office buildings;
O    office furnitture and equipment;
O    communications and data-processing equipment;
O    vehicles;
o    st.ocks and stores; and
Cl   service facilities.
Standard valuation practices should be used in
establishing the  current monetary valve   of these
assets.
2.1.5.    Land
With respect to buildings and other   installations
occupying land, the value of such land should be
appropriately incorporated. Costs or valuations of
such lend and of rights over, on or under land,
should include appropriate valuations of land
already in the public domain. Unused land, in the
Corporation's  ownership,    should  be   similarly
valued.
2.2. jasurance
As soon as the identification and valuation of any
significant part of the Corporation's assets have been
completed, the consultant should report this to the
Corporation, together with his recommendation as to
which assets should immediately be insured against
damage and/or public liability risks. The valver should
also be prepared to suggest suitable policies and
covers for the Corporation's consideration.
2.3.   ssseto_ibitS
The  Corporation   has  assurned   a  large  number   of
liabilities as the successor to MOWD undertakings in
operating and implementing water supply systems. In
addition, in its own right, the Corporation has been
assuming new current liabilities, as well as potential
long-term and contingent liabilities as it performs its
mandated responsibilities.



-61-                            Annex 9
Page 6 of 32
The magnitvde of the inherited and newly arising
liabilities has not yet been fully determined. Thus,
the consultant is required to identify and assess the
value of all:
O    inherited liabilities;
O    current contractual and other liabilities; and
O    potential   and  contingent   liabilities  that  may
arise in the course of the Corporation's execution
of its services.
In making the identifications and assessments, the
consultant is reqvired to advise the Corporation on the
extent and likelihood of possible claims, either for
settlement or indemnification.
2.s.1    El. I Ete _Iiabilities
As the successor to MOWD in respect of operational
water undertakings, the Corporation has legally
assumed some of the liabilities obtaining at the
water supplies prior to 1st July, 1989. The
principal   liabilities  in   this  connection   are
expected to consist of:
O    cont-actors' and consultants' claims;
O    suppliers unpaid invoices;
O    consumers water deposits   and claims on water
accounts; and
O    wayleaves and   unsettled claims   arising from
past developments.
The  consultant    is   expected   to    provide   a
comprehensive   listing  of these   liabilities  and
their value for each water undertaking under the
Corporation's charge as at 1st. Jvly, 1989.
2.3.2.             iCk.lJties
Since its incorporation, the Corporation has been
ga'ining additional liabili.ies arising from the
development of new water facilities, continued
provision   of   water   services   in   operational
schemes,   establishment    and   growth    of   the
Corporation, acquisition of personnel, provision
of supportive services, etc.
These current and growing liabilities are of two
main forms - contractual obligations and potential
or contingent liabilities. These both carry risks
and may be suitable for indemnity considerations
and insurance coverase.

ONGOING ACCOUNTING AND FINANCIAL REPORTING
3.1. As described in Section 1, the Corporation will have to
est.ablish, report and submit, for audit, its initial
financial position, based on the Statement of Affairs
to be prepared as a result of the valuations of this
consultancy.
3.2. Thereafter, for each svbwequent account.ing period,  the
Corporation will be required to keep its accounts and
to prepare its financial reports, in accordance with
generally accepted accovnting principles, applicable to
commercial organizations.
3.3. These accounting principles prescribe that depreciation
be charged, periodically, in the accounts and reported
upon in the annual financial statements. Whilst methods
for doing this may differ in detail, the most common
standard practice used in the accounting profession is
to charge and to record depreciation on the "straight-
line" method. This method would require to be based
upon a declaration cf a "gross" value of each category
of the fixed assets, against which there would be
annual charges, based on assessed working lives and
likely disposal values.
3.4. For the purposes of this valuation, the "gross" values
of the assets should be an assessment of what they
would have cost, when new, revalued to allow for
changing money values since they were put into service.
Assessment of the current asset valves, in accordance
with   this   consultancy,   would   then   become,  for
accounting purposes, the declared "net" values. The
difference between the "gross" and the "net" values
would   then   be,  bv   definition,    the  accumulated
depreciation.
3.5. However, the Corporation fully appreciates that, for
this consultancy, it will be possible only to make
approximate assessments in this matter. Furthermore, it
may be that only credible "net" values can be declared,
egainst which future deprecietion will then be charged.
3.6. Whatever position is arrived at, resulting from the
above  assessments,   it  will   be  necessary  for  the
consultants   to  present    the   Corporation  with   a
methodology for its ongoing depreciation charges, both
to conform to its mandated accounting requirements and
also   for   management    accounting   purposes.   This
methodology should include a schedule of appropriate
depreciation rates to be used, by whatever method
recommended.



-63-                           Annex 9
Page 8 of 32
3.7. In   addition  t.o  it's  legally mandated    reporting
requirements,  the Corporation will  wish, for  its own
management purposes, to make periodic assessments of
the rate of return on the investment of its funds in
operating assets, to compare with its costs of capital.
Furthermore,  since public  funding is involved,  it is
appropriate for such an assessment to be compared with
any imputed  real (economic)  costs of  capital to  the
Kenya  economy. In addition,  such assessments might be
required to be reported to outside investors, including
international financing entities, as part of their
conditionality  in rmiaking  funds available  for   the
Corporation 's capital investment program.
3.8. Whilst currently prevailing accounting practices, for
the purposes of legal reporting and auditing, do not
necessarily provide for annual revaluation of assets,
rate of return assessments can only be credible if they
incorporate annual "net" fixed asset values and related
depreciation charges which are based on current values.
3.9. This consultancy should,   therefore, recommend  simple
ond inexpensive procedures, whereby, after the initial
establishment of the values of the fixed assets, these
may   be   periodically   revalued  for   purposes   of
calculation of rates of return. It is recognized that
such valuations may not necessarily be incorporated
within such of the Corporation's accounts and financiel
reports as may be prepared for other purposes. They
may, however, be presented as supplements to the annual
financial stat.ements.
4.   PERSONNEL REQUIREMENTS
4.1. The tasks defined in Section 2, above, indicate that
this valuation  consultency needs a  sufficiently large
and varied corps of professional staff, fully competent
and experienced in the followirng dornsans of expertise:
(a)  valuation, of:
O    land and wayleeves;
O    plant, machinery and equipment;
O    water pipelines and fittings;
O    buildings and site works;
O    water retaining structures;
O    moveable office furniture and equipment;
o    electronic         data-processing        and
telecommunications equipment;
0    stocks and stores;
(b) water engineering;



-64-                        Annex 9
Page 9 of 32
(c)  land curvey;
(d)  insurance;
(e)  accounting and finance4
(f)  law,  including that  relating to  insurance, real
property,     contract,     tort.    and    pvblic
administration; end,
(g)  management   of   water    retaining   structures,
including siltation end safety inspections.
4.2. Hence, the consultency will be expected to assemble
competent, experienced and qualified multi-disciplinary
team,  comprising,   as  a   minimum,  all   the  above
disciplines.   There  must  also  be  a  competent  and
efficient management and communication st.ructure to
facilitate the teamwork necessary for the successful
execution of the specified tesks.
4.3. For some of the activities, Kenya's law or professional
practices may require that certain public declerations
be made (or particular documentation certified) only by
professionals qualified by examination or license. This
may apply, for example, to lawyers, accountants and
valuers. The Corporation will require the names end
credentials of such persons, together with all other
registered professionals expected to participate.
S.   DURATION
S.1. Time is of the essence for this consultanlcy, as many of
the on-going mctivities of the Corporation will be
effected by its results. The urgency for the insurance
for insurable assets  and indemnifiable liabilities  is
self-evident.  The findings  of this consultency   will
also form important inputs into the preparation of the
Corporationi's annual financial statements for 1992/93,
which closea on  30th June, 1993. Such  statements will
be   necessary  for  the   Corporation  to  affirm   its
financial credibility and credentials to the Goverinment
and to potential investors, including international
financing entities.
5.2. With  these considerations in mind, a maximum pemiod of
9 calendar months is proposed, of which 6 months may be
utilized  for field work,  with t.he remainder reserved
for renport-writing.

behalf of the Corporat.ion, by a teami of Joint Lead

the  }ey  staff  who  may be   contacted  by  the  Lead

6.3. An inception report, detailing how provision of the
various services has been initiated, explaining the
extent  to which  the  financial  end  time  budget   is
expected  to be  adhered  to, and  suggesting  poss4ble
modifications in task execvtion, shall be submitted one
month after the commencement of services.
6.4. Thereafter, monthly progress reports shell be submitted
and regular briefing meetings arranged as needed by the
Joint   Lead   Consultants.  Interim   reports   should
concentrate on the presentation of information which
can be incorporated into  the Corporation's records end
activities. Reference to the administration of the work
should be minimized, preferably confined t.o exception
reports.
6.6. A  full Interim Report shall be submitted not, late then
31st December, 1992. The Draft Final Report shall be
available  on 31st. Janvary, 1993, with the Final Report
submitted nr,- later then 30th April, 1993.
6.S. The Finel Report shmll comprise:
o    an executive summory of the principal findings and
recoinmendeticns;
O    an  aggregated statement of affairs,   showing the
assets, liablitiec and equity capital of the
Corporation as n whole;
o    a   statement   of   the   insurable  asseto   and
liabilities of the Corporation, accompsnied by
suggetions and recommendationn on various options
f or insurance and indemn3ty;
O    appendices on the  variouts assets and  liabilities
for each wnter vndert kang; nnd
o    appendices on  the detailed  methodologies applied
an  valuation  of assets    and  determinntion  of
liabilities.

TERMS OF REFERENCE
FOR
THE JOINT LEAD CONSULTANTS
FOR VALUATION OF ASSETS/LIABILITIES
1     Review the Terms of Reference for the valuation of assets and liabilities, and
comment on them. These comments should be addressed to the NWCPC particularly
in those areas if any where the TOR need to be changed or strengthened;
2     Approve the suitability of consulting personnel proposed by each of the contracted
consulting firms to undertake the various tasks of the TOR for which they have been
proposed;

C.

IMPROVEMENT OF REVENUE COLLECTION

1,   BACKGROUND
1.1. Since the  early seventies,   the  Government of  Kenya,
through the Mlinistry of Water Development, has invested
heavily in the development of both rural and urban
water  projects. In this direction, the Government has
vigorously endeavored to provide easily accessible
water to Kenya's growing rural end urban population for
domestic, institutional commercial and agricultural
use.
1.2. It is  estimated that  by 1990,   six million  rural and
urban residents were being served with potable water.
Furthermore, average distances travelled by members of
rural households in search of safe water had beers
reduced  considerably   by  1990.   In  spite  of  these
worthwhile development efforts, svbstantial additional
investments are needed to realize the Government long-
term objectives of providing good quality water in
sufficient quantities and at close proximity to all.
2.   ESTABLISHMENT OF THE NATIONAL WATER CONSERVATION &   PIPELINE
CORPORATION
In the late eighties, the Government of Kenya became
increasingly concerned with lack of effective management and
poor financial performance of    both rural  and urban  water
supply. The concern thereof led the Government to establish
the National Water ConservatLon and Pipeline Corporation as
a vehicle to introduce svitable reforms in financial and
operations and maintenence management of water supplies. The
Corporation so established became operational on lst. July,
19B9 and has in its portfolio 24 operational water supplies,
including the Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply.
3.   OVERALL PROJECT OBJECTIVE
The principal objectives of the Improvement. of Revenue
Collection, Financial Management and Management Information
System Project are to improve revenue collection, develop
sound accounting procedures and implement a comprehensive
management. information system that will be responsive to the
functional end administrative needs of the Corporation.

D.
TERMS OF REFERENCE
NATIONAL WATER CONSERVATION AND
PIPELINE CORPORATION
CORPORATE DEVELOPMENT PLAN
1,0     BACKGROUND
1.1     In the late 1805, the Government of Kenya became increasingly
concerned with the lack of effective management and poor financial
performance of both rural and urban water supplies. The concern thereof
led the 6overnment to establish the National Water Conservation and
Pipeline Corporation as a vehicle to introduce suitable reforms in
financial and operations and maintenance management of water supplies.     The
Corporation so established became operational on 1st. July, 1989, and has
in its portfolio 24 operational water supplies, including the Mombasa and
Coastal Water Supply.
1.2     Even prior to the formal commencement of its activities in July
1989, the corporation had identified the neea for a Corporate Planning
capability to assist its management. To fulfill its mandate, the
Corporation needs systematic, coordinated and integrated planning,
involving all of its departments and operations. The establishment, in May
1990, of a Corporate Services Department was intended to facilitate this.
2.0     THE WATER SUPPLY SECTOR
2.1     Among the more important matters which the Government of Kenya must
address within the nation's water sector are the following:
(a) overall development and Management of water resources and the
allocation of these resources to Meet a variety of concerns;
(b) agricultural irrigation and rtural development;
(c) abstraction, treatment, delivery and sale of potable water, for
domestic, commercial, industrial and public purposes;
(d) provision of rural water supplies, principally for domestic
consumption, at affordable prices which will not necessarily
cover costs, thereby performing a social and public health
function), intended to benefit the rural poor;
(e) protection of the natural environment, including the conservation
of water to sustain wildlife; and
(f) oublic sanitation with either on-plot or mains sewerage as well
as other aspects sf wastewater disposal.



-75-                           Annex 9
Page 20 of 32
2.2     Prior to the establishment of the Corporation, many of these
matters were the responsibility of the Ministry of Water Development (MWD).
Since the inception of the Corporation, some of these responsibilities are
now shared.
2.3     Within the larger towns, with the notable exception of Mombasa, the
delivery end sale of potable water for domestic, commercial, industrial and
public purposes has been - and continues to be - principally a municipal
responsibility. Urban sewage disposal has also been a municipal service.
2.4     However, MWD was responsible for domestic, commercial, industrial
and public water supply services:
(a) for the Coast Region, including Mombasa;
(b) for small urban and rural centers; and
(c) as a bulk supplier of water to municipalities, either as the
sole source of supply or as a supplement to the local sources.
2.5     Following the Corporation's establishment in 1988, these specific
Ministry functions were transferred to the Corporation, for the areas
legally designated.
3.0     THE MANDATE AND PURPOSE OF THE CORPORATIOr'
3.1     The Corporation's present mandate is to manage and develop the
water projects legally entrusted to it, including the supply of bulk and
retail water within those project areas. Its mandate also includes the
responsibility to assist the Government in the formulation and execution of
a national water policy.
3.2     Implicit in the selection of the responsibilities transferred to
the Corporation, taken together with the policy of the Government, is the
requirement that the Corporation will operate on a fully commercial basis,
covering all of its costs and contributng substantially towards its
investment programs from funds rjenerated from its operations.
3.3     However, the Corporation, whilst dealing with a vital national
resource, cannot be seen to be doing so in isolation from other national
concerns for water development, conservation and use. Thus, the
Corporation, presently( a fledgling institution, wishes to establish a clear
and distinct role for itself which will optiMize its contribution to the
sector, without compromising its requirement to operate commercially.
3.4     The Corporation will, therefore, expect to take over for
construction and operation such schemes as can be declared in the future to
be within its legal, technical, economic, financial and managerial



Annex 9
-76-                           Page 21 of 32
conpetence. In the course of time, this night include, but in any case not
be linited to, any or all of the schemes currently operated independently
by municipalities and MWO.
4.0     OBJECTIVES OF THE STUDY
4.1     The objectives of the study are four-fold:    (1) to undertake a
water sector study (delineation study) in order to more clearly define and
distinguish the Corporation's role in the water sector from other agencies
responsible for water supplies and sanitation services; and (2) to prepare
a S-Year Corporate Development Plan, based on the expected role of the
Corporation over the medium term, including an investment and financing
plan and policies, (3) to develop a planning capability within the
Corporation; and (4' to undertake a water tariff study that will lead to a
tariff structure and tariff levels that will ensure a commercially
succeosful future for the Corporation.
5.0     WATER SECTOR STUDY
S.1     In order to provide a framework for identifying needed strategies
and policies and a clearer delineation of responsibilities for the
Corporation, it is necessary to undertake a background study of the water
sector. This should include, but not be limited to:
(a) a review of the historical development of the water sector
since 1950S
(b) an overview of past problems in the water sector, with respect
to finance, personnel and social reach;
tc) a general review of the performance of existing water supply,
sanitation and sewerage schemes;
(d) a review of technological appropriateness and importance of
engineering design criteria and their application in existing
water supply schemes5
(e) a review of the causes of past poor operational performance of
water supply, sanitation and sewerage schemes;
(f) a review of the constraints placed on scheme performance by poor
or inadequate maintenancet
(g) a review of the effects of Government policies upon the
activities of the Ministry of Water Development, municipalities
and of the Corporation;



-77-                           Annex 9
Page 22 of 32
(h) a review of the effects of Government policies on the planning,
construction and management of water supply, sanitation and
sewerage services in the country; and
(i) an assessment of likely future concerns arising in the sector,
towards the resolution of which the Corporation might be expected
to contribute.
To assist the Corporation in placing the review in perspective, the
Consultant should draw on the experience of similar institutions in other
developing countries.
5.2     From the results of the review carried out above and the experience
of similar institutions, the Consultant should develop recommendations
concerning:
(a) the delineation of activities among the Ministry, the
Corporation and the municipalitiesi
(b) policy changes required to harmonize development and manage-
ment of water supply, sanitation and sewerage projects in the
country and how and when such changes should be instituted;
{c) reforms relating to existing rural water supply projects, to
improve their long-term performance, including review of scope
for greater community participation and district focus;
(d) strategies to be adopted for further development of urban and
rural water supply schemes.
6.0     S-YEAR CORPORATE DEVELOPMENT PLAN
6.1     Based on the Corporation's current responsibilities, the Consultant
in liaison with the Corporation should prepare a five-year Corporate
Development Plan The Corporate Development Plan would be expected to
include, but not be limited to:
(a) a clear definition of the Corporation's aims and objectives
over the medium term;
(b) identification of the priority activities, policies and
operational and financial targets to be achieved over the same
time period;
(c) recommendations on the proposed management organizatLon
required to carry out the plani
(d) identification of a specific 5-year investment plan along with



-78-                          Annex 9
Page 23 of 32
a propoeed financing plan which ctnsiders the Corporation's
requirements for maintenance and operations as well as the
likely revenujes and requirements for outside borrowings;
(a) a manpower development plan which would help to ensure that the
appropriate manpower skills are available in order to properly
implement the plan; and
(f) an assets and liabilities management plan.
7.0     DEVELOPMENT OF A CORPORATE PLANNING CAPABILITY
7.1     Elaaning.   Using the initial recommendations as a starting point,
the Consultant should advi6e on the staffing and organization of the
ongoing corporate planning function, most probably centered on the
development of the Corporate Planning Division within the Corporate
Services Department.
7.2     It is also expected that it will be necessary to establish a Joint
Planning Panel. This Panel is likely to be the forum for the exchange of
information and opinions among the various senior managers of the
Corporation. It will be likely chaired by the Chief Corporate Services
Manager and include the following functions:
(a) ensuring that the allocation and utilization of available
resources are rational and systematic;
(b) providing a continuous link among the various operational and
administrative departments; and
(c) providing a mechanism for ieriodic, formal joint reviews of
the Corporate Development Plan, whereby it can be kept contin-
uously updated and current, consistent with newly available
information.
7.3     ProoranMino and Bjudgjtin.   Actions to be taken as a result of the
corporate planning process cannot be expected to be meaningful unless
related to the availability and timing of resources.    The Corporate
Development Plan must, therefore, be related to policies which incorporate
such resources, including but not limited to financial resources.    Actions
will therefore need to be planned and scheduled within a strategic multi-
year programming and budgeting system, extending far beyond the immediate
formulation of single-year administrative budgets.
7.4     These programs and budgets, to which the plans relate, Thould not
be mere funding allocations. Instead, they should be related h' the need
for - and the potential availability of - human and material resources.
Emphasis should be placed on how such resources will be organized, within
the Corporation, to effect the desired results.



Annex 9
-79-                         'Page 24 of 32
7.5     Furthermore, regard should alsc be given to the eAternal
administrative environrment within which the Corporation must operate.   Many
decisions to be taken in this wider environment will be beyond the
Corporation's direct control. These decl5lons are, however, capable of
being influenced by the Corporation, provided that they are anticipated
well enough in advance.   Thi5 must also form part of the planning and
programming process. Based on these considerations, the Consultant will be
expected to provide recommendations for institutionalizing an appropriate
planning, programming and budgeting process within the Corporation.
8.13    WATER TARIFF STUDIY
8.1     As indicated above, the implementation of actions under the
corporate plan will depend significantly upon the availability of financial
resources. This, in turn, will relate to the potential of the Corporation
to generate funds from its operations and to raise eA.ternal capital.
8.2     This generation of internal and e>ternal funds must be grounded iii
the profitability and financial integri-ty of the Corporation, which as a
financially autonomous enterprise will relate significantly to its pricing
policies.
8.3     It can be taken for granted that the Corporation and the Government
are both closely and continuously concerned with the need to increase the
general level of tariffs and charges for the Corporation's services, given
the present relatively unsatisfactory level of financial performance.
d3.4    However, merely increasing the general level of prices does not
address the issue of whether the design of the tariff structure is the most
efficient for the maximization of revenue, equity, administrative
convenience and cost of collection. Furthermore, glven the imminent
necessity for significant increases in the general tariff level, it is
necessary to pay particular attention to the issues of public and political
acceptability and perceptions of fairness.
8.5     The Consultant is, therefore, requested to examine the present
tariff structujre and to consider and report upon its general suitability
and applicability to the concerns of the Corporation, indicating any
serious shortcomings which require to be remedied. The Consultant should
consider and provide recommendations on, but not necessarily be limited to,
the following:
(a) the definitions of consumer classifications: between rural
and urban; and among residential, commercial, industrial,
hotel and governmental customers,
(b) the cost of providing service to each consumer class: costs
should (i) differentiate between direct and indirect costs and



Annex 9
-80-                            Page 25 of 32
(ii) be calculated separately on (1) the traditional basis,
using the revalued cost of asset5 u3ed to provide service and
(2) the marginal cost ba5s5, 4sing the cost of incremental
water supply over the mediurm  to lonc term;
(c) the subsidy provided each customer class based on currerntly
effective tariffs;
(d) the appropriateness of uniform urban and uniform rural tariff
structures versus regional urban and rural tariff structures or
individual town/rural area tariff structures;
(e) the appropriateness of crcss-subsadies through the tariff levels
and structures across and within regions;
(f) the ability to introduce more economically and financially
efficient tariff 5tructure5 taking into consideration the cost
of provision of service to, and elastlcity of demand of,
government, hotel, industrial, commercial and domestic
consumers wtihin schemes and regions; and
(g) ways and moeans to protect the needs of the low income groups
through the tariff structure.

INTRODUCTION
1.    The National Water Conservation and Pipeline Corporation requires the services of a
firm of Consulting Engineers to provide Coordination/Liaison/Management Consultancy and
Advisory Services for the Second Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Engineering and
Rehabilitation Project. This project is to proceed with the assistance of the World Bank and
will involve a wide range of complementary services provided by various consultants from
several countries and covering several related disciplines.
2.    To coordinate these various activities and to liaise between the Client (Project
Coordinator), the consultants and the funding agency(s) requires the services of an
organization experienced in the field of water supply with knowledge of Kenya and of
working with international funding agencies.
SCQPE SQF F.QKSORQQOORDINATIQN
3.    Under the Second Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Engineering and Rehabilitation
Project, activities are to proceed under three principle headings, namely;-
(i)      Institutional Improvement and Capacity Building;
(ii)      Rehabilitation and Augmentation of the earlier Mombasa and Coastal
Water Supply Projects (Sabaki Water Project and 1st Mzima Pipeline),
and immediate improvement measures in the distribution systems in the
coastal region.
(iii)     Pre-investment Studies and Engineering for a follow-on Second
Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Project.
4.    Activities to be coordinated, reviewed and liaised under (i) would include (but not
necessarily limited to):
* the valuation of all recently acquired assets and liabilities of the National Water
Conservation and Pipeline Corporation comprising some 43 water supply systems,
25 of which are under operation and 18 are under various stages of development
and extension;
* the preparation of an opening balance sheet including recommendations for
ensuring an adequate capital structure;
* improvement of revenue collection to be achieved through a series of inter-related
measures including;

all procedures necessary for meter reading, billing and revenue collection;
staff training for future consumer surveys and for operating of the improved
systems;
leak detection studies.

in the Coastal Region.
* Improvement of financial systems and the establishment of a management
information system which will include:-
-   improving of budgeting procedures, accounting, procurement and control systems;

and in the vicinity of Voi;
* augmentation works to increase output levels of the Sabaki Water Project, most
probably by the development of groundwater under die North Bank of the Sabaki
river, a short distance upstream of the Baricho Intake, by the sinking of upto 4
wells, and the conveyance of water across the river to Baricho;

the Sabaki Water Project which would include, but not necessarily limited to:

water plant treatment;
-   refurbishment of components along the transmission main, installation of limited
additional clear water storage reservoir at Nguu Tatu and of branch lines;
-   construction and installation of new booster pumping station;
-   improvements to the telecommunication system.

(under KFW financing) and is presently engaged on a hydraulic model study of the Baricho

a two well wellfield under the South Bank of the Sabaki River and for limnited improvement

Works.

A.
TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR CONSULTANCY SiRVICES FOR
SUDY AND DESIGN TO INCREASE BULK WATER SUPPLY FOR
T1E SECOND MOMBASA AND COASTiAL WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
A.    Background
1.   The Mombasa and Coastal Water supply system, serving a 1990 population
of about 1,640,000 and having a supply area of approximately 5,700 sq. km,
is the second largest regional water supply scheme in Kenya, and supplies
by far the largest area.
2.   The overall responsibility for tne water supply in the Mombasa and Coastal
Region (which rested until recently with the Ministry of Water Development)
was transferred to the newly formed National Water Resources and Pipeline
Corporation established in 1988 under the State Corporation Act (Cap 446)
Section 3 by Legal Notice No.270 of 19C,8.
3.   The supply is in urgent need of attention both to increase the total water
supply volume as demand already exceeds capacity of existing source and
transmission-works, and also to improve the water distribution system(s) in
the supply area.
4.    Following and also simultaneously with the implementation of the last
extension project (Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Project,1975-1982)
a number of studies were carried out to identify alternatives for further source
work extensions. The most comprehensive of these studies was the
"Feasibility Study on Water Supply Augmentation Project of Moimbasa -
Coastal Area Hinterland" (JICA, 1981).
5.    Even prior to the formal commencement of its activities in July, 1989, NWCPC
reviewed the various alternatives for the source work d&velopments, and
identified, as the most viable option for providing additional water to
Mombasa in the shortest possible time, the increased abstraction from
Mzima Springs, one of the existing sources ("Second Mzima Pipeline
Project). As a result of interest evident during 1988, NWCPC in collaboration
with its Consultant, drew up an "Invitation for Firm Proposals for Engineering
and Design Services, Construction of the Works and Financing" for the
second Mzima Pipeline. As this 'turnkey' approach did not materialize, and
also keeping in mind that,the second Mzima project alone would not provide
an adequate amount to eliminate the deficit in supply, it has now been
decided to follow a two-phased approach.
6.   The National Water Conservation and Pipeline Corporation, with the support
of the Government of Kenya, and in consultation with the Ministry of Water
Development, decided that short and long term plans are to be prepared for
the expansion of the water supplies to Mombasa and the Coastal Region



Annex 10
-89-                           Page 2 of 37
under an engineering and rehabilitation project,followed by a phased
implementation of these development plans. NWCPC intends to meet these
commitments during the planning and implementation stages with financial
assistance from international development agencies under guarartee from
the Government of the Republic of Kenya (GOK).
7.   It has also been decided that the first phase project ("Second Mombasa and
Coastal Region Water Supply Engineering and lRehabilitatibn Project") will
provide Interalla for (a) the preparation (engineering)and implementation of
rehabilitation/augmentabon measures, to allow for near term improvements
and (b) for studies and engineering required for medium and long term
Improvements (i.e. preparation of the next main investment project). These
preparatory works will be carried out under separate consultancy
assignments with respect to (i) sourcework developments, (i) distribution
network improvements and extension,and (iii) specialized services for control
and tele-communication system(s). NWCPC also intends to retain
independent consultants for project coordination/liaison/maragement
services.
8.   The consultancy services under this Terms of Reference are in respect of
study and design of bulk water supply. The following sectons describe the
objectives of this assignment the scope of work and general guidellnes,and
specific guidelines for carrying out the services. It also Includes the tme frame
for the services and the sources of information as known by NWCPC.
S.   Objectives And Approach
I1.  Built upon the previous studies the NWCPC wishes to pursue the next major
expansion of the water supply facilities for Mombasa and the Coastal Region.
It is intended that the expansion of source works will satisfy the requirements
In the supply area until the year 2010. As it is recognised by NWCPC that the
optimal development of the sources of supply (including those previously
identified and other possible sources) does not necessarily coincide with a
set design horizon,the consultants shall propose a phased development
plan with the main objective being that the present water deficit in the supply
area shall be reduced as early as possible.
2.   In accordance with the main objective set above, the consultancy assignment
will be carried out in the following phases:
Phase 1
(i)   The inital stage of phase 1 shall include the review and update of all
existing  previous studies, reports, and proposals relating to the
existing souirces and relating to source works developments
(including studies, reports, and proposals prepared by NWCPC and
other government agencies), with special regard to the proposed.
Second Mzima Project. This review will also include an initial
assessment of environmental impacts of the studied alternatives. It is
expected that this stage will conclude with the formulation of the
source works development component (Project Definition) of the
follow-on main investment project, which shall also provide for



Annex 10
-90-                            Page 3 of 37
additional investigations for source development for the long-term.
(i)   The second stage of phase 1, after review and approval of the of
phased development plan and the selected atternative(s)for the next
major investment project uShort-Term Implementation Plan' will
comprise the pr!iminary engineering (layout) design, detailed
environmental impact assessment of the proposed components, the
preparaton of a draft environmental action programme and refined
project cost estimate.
Phase 2
(i)   Detailed engineering designs, contract packaging, preparation of bid
documents, pre-qualification of Contractors (as required) and
preparation of final environmental action programme.
(ii)  Assistance to NWCPC during appraisal of the main investment project
by the lending agencies.
(iii) Evaluation of bids.

B.
TERMS OF REFERENCE FOR CONSULTANCY SERVICES FOR
DISTRIBUTION NETWORKS' IMPROVEMENT AND EXTENSION
FOR THIE SECOND MOMBASA AND COASTAL WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
A.    Backtground
1.   The Mombasa and Coastal Water supply system, serving a 1990 population of
about 1,640,000 and having a supply area of approximately 5,700 sq.km, is the
second largest regional water supply scheme in Kenya, and supplies by far the
largest area.
2.   The overall responsibility for the water supply in the Mombasa and Coastal
Region (which rested until recently with the Ministry of Water Development) was
,-insferred to the newly formed National Watar Conservation and Pipeline
Corporation established in 1988 under the State Corporation Act (Cap 446)
Section 3 by Legal Notice No. 270 of 1988.
3.    The supply is in. urgent need of attention both to increase the total water supply
volume as demand already exceeds capacity of existing source and
transmission-works, and also to Improve the water distribution system(s) In the
supply area.
4     .Following and also simultaneously with the implementation of the last extension
project (Mombasa and Coastal Water Supply Project, 1975 - 1982) a number of
studies were carried out to Identify alternatives for further source work
extensions. The most comprehensive of these studies was the "Feasibility Study
on Water Supply Augmentaton Project of Mombasa - Coastal Area Hllnteritnan
(JICA, 1981).
5.    Even prior to the. formal commencement of Its activities in July, 1989, NWCPC
reviewed the various afternatives for the source work developments, and
Identified, as the most viable option for providing additional water to Mombasa
In the sh6rtest possible time, the increased abstraction from Mzima Springs, one
of the exing sources ("Second Mzima Pipeline Projec). As a result of interest.
evident durIng 1988, NWCPC in collaboration with its Consultant, drew up an
ilnvitation for Firm Proposals for Engineering and Design Services, Construction
of the Works and Financing" for the second Mzima Pipeline. As this 'turnkey'
approach did not materialize, and also keeping in mind that, the second Mzima
project aj would not provide an adequate amount to eliminate the deficit in
supply, it has now been decided to follow a two-phased approach.
S.    The National Water Conservation and. Pipeline Corporation, with the support of
the Government of Kenya, and in consultation with the Ministry of Water
Development, decided that short and long term plans are to be prepared for thq
expansion of the water supplies to Mombasa and the Coastal Region under an
engineering and rehabilitation project, followed by a phased Implementation of



99                        Annex 10
Page 12 of 37
these development plans. NWCPC intends to meet these commitments during
the planning and Implementation stages with financial assistance from
international development agencies under guarantee from the Government of
the Republic of Kenya (GOK).
7     .It has also been decided that the first phase project ('Second, Mornbasa and
Coastal Region Water Supply Engineering and Rehabilitation Project') will
provide interalia for
(a)  the  preparation   (engineering)  and  implarrientation  of
rehabilitation/augmentation measures, to allow for near term improveiennts andc
(b) for studies and engineering required for medium and long term
improvements (i.e. preparation of the next main investment project). These
preparatory works will be carried out under separate consultancy assignments
with respect to (i) sourcework developments, (ii) distribujtion network
improvements and extension, and (iii) specialized services for control and
tele-cornmunication system(s). NWCPC also intends to retaini independent
consultants for project coordination/liaison/management services.
8.   The consultancy services under this Terms of Reference are in respect of
distribution network improvement and extension. The follow,ving sections
describe the objectives of this assignment, the scope of work and general
guidelines, and specific guidelines for carrying out the services. It also includes
the time-frame of the services and the sources of information as known by
NWCPC.
B.   Objectives and Approach
1.   The National Water Conservation and Pipeline Corporation (NWCPC) wishes to
pursue the improvement and expansion of water supply facilities for Mombasa
and the Coastal Region. It is intended that in addition to the expansion of source
works, a systematic improvement and extension of the distribution systems
(including the transmission mains and the regional trunk distribution system) will
be carried out, to ensure adequate water survey to the consumers up to tie year
2000 and beyond.
2.   In accordance with the main objective set above, -the Consultants shall review
all aspect6 of equitable distribution of water to the consumers. The work should
be carried out in a manner that would allow the NWCPC to provide Improvement
to the consumers in the near term (immediate rehabilitation measures), In the
short term up to year 2010 (follow-on main investment project), and would also
facilitate the planning and design for long-term expansion.
3     .In order to improve the water supply in Mombasa and the Coastal Region in the
near-term and satisfy the demands in the short-term, It is necessary to optimise
the performance of the existing facilities, Including rehabilitation, red.ction of
physical losses and unaccounted-for-water, Improvements and modiflcations,
and to improve the metering of the consumption.



-100-                     Annex 10
Page 13 of 37
4.    The increase in the volume of water borne waste (principally domestic sewage,
but also Industrial effluents) associated with the Increase In water demand
require the waste dlsposal systems to be expanded. it will be necessary to
assessthe present status of waste water disposal (and sanitation) and to Identify
the need for a future expansion of Mombasa's sewage system as well as the
measures required in other urban areas in the Coastal Region.

3.2   Leak Detection and Leakage Control
At present, no active leakagF control monitoring is in force. Leakage control
and repair is passive and based on physical visual leakages observed and
reported. Due to the aged transmission and distribution systems, leakage is
expected substantial. However, no adequate figures can be given due to the



Annex 10
-107-                        Page 20 of 37
unreliability of production figures and consumer billed consumptions. As
leakage represents a wastage of resources, inefficient operation and
rraintenance due to financial constraints, NWCPC decided thiat in the future a
systematic approach shall be followed regarding detection and leakage control.
rhe consultant, therefore, shall prepare proposals, and carry out as pait of the
assignment the following services, which should cover, Include, but not
necessarily limited to the topics described below.
/a)   Study the alternative leakage control state-of-the-art methods. The
methods should be practical considering the prevailing conditions in the
network. These studies should include the resources required for each
and the costs of implementing leakage control.
'kb)  Collection, collation and analysis of production and consumption data in
order to estimate leakage levels from existing data. The consultants will
be expected to allow for meter errors and give due cornsideration to the
estimated consumptions on stopped or under-registering meters.
Exception reports from the existing billing system should be analyzed
historically in order to see the trends and get any meaningful correlation.
The need for a practical and specialised leakage control Engineer is
paramount for this analysis.
'c)   Proposals for measurement of leakage for the various components of the
systems reservoirs, transmission mains, and on the clistribution system
should be determined appropriately to determine their relative
magnitudes. In oLtaining this information, there will be need to:-
i)    Study of the existing network to determine suitability of location of
macro-metering.
ii)   For suitable flow controls suitable flow measuring equipment and
Instrumentation should be recommended for installation for:-
* continuous flow recording and automatic digital data logger units at
measuring stations;
* assessment of net night flows;
* assessment of amount of leakage and of its increase/decrease;
* assessment of approximate area of network leakage through aaalysis of
day to day flow variations.
(d)   Recommernd suitable leak detection, location, and pipe locator
equipment bearing in mind the materials of the pipes, cost implications
and the nature of the long transmission mains. Consideration In
recommendations for such equipmrent or method should Include
operational requirements and training needed; availability of repair and
maintenance facilities, cadre and number of manpower requirements,
vehicular requirements, and conditions of the water supplies. Due



Annex 10
-'08~                        Page 21 of 37
consideration should be given to the low pressure situations particularly
within the distribution system and the sometimes intermittent supply
situation.
'xe)  Proposals for determination of the leakage levels shall be given in
consideration of data from exisling data and the measurement of the
leakage.
'4)   Calculation of the unit cost of leakage to give the economic benefits
accruing either through increased revenue or as reduction in operating
costs or deferment of capital expenditure resulting from the saving of
water as a consequence of leakage control measures.
(,g) As the main objective is to reduce the unaccounted-for-water, estimates
should be made of the reduction in leakage with the different control
programmes. Estirnates of expected leakage reductions should be made
with a view to setting up leakage reduction targets.
t4i)  The annual cost of leakage and leakage control should be worked out
for each method proposed.
(4)  Selection of the method which provides the greatest net benefit in
economic terms should finally be recommended taking into account local
factors while considGring benefits provided by some methods which may
be difficult to quantify in economic terms.
(:J)  As a final measure a leakage control policy should be recommended
implementation. The stages of implementation should be specified
depending on the met,lod recommended. Such stages may Include but
not limited to
Site and flow surveys to determine the most suitable meter locations;
. Installation of meters;
Operation of meter system to measure leakage levels;
Establishing and training of leak detection and repair gangs to reduce
leakage levels.
/Jc)  Finally the proposals for regular monitoring to determine the performance
